Addressing the Opposition on Space and Direction
The author addresses two specific objections from the opponent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two objections raised against the author's position and how he refutes them, including the distinction between essential and spatial separation.

Core Idea
The terms 'separation' and 'distinction' are ambiguous: they can mean essential difference without space or spatial difference with space.

The opponent raises two objections: first, that space and direction are not real things; second, that when the opponent says 'mubayin' he only means essential distinction. The author responds decisively. He first asserts that space and direction are real, proven by conclusive arguments. Then he analyzes the ambiguity of terms like 'infirad' and 'imtiyaz', showing that the opponent's intended meaning (spatial) leads to a need for space, which is impossible for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage of responses
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read its translation. Notice the two 'Ammā' (أما) sections marking the two objections.
2
Identify the two objections and their responses
First: space and direction are not real. Second: the terms only mean essential distinction. The author answers each in order.
The second objection is more subtle; look at the ambiguity argument.
3
Understand the distinction between essential and spatial separation
The author explains that words like 'infirad' can refer to essential difference (no direction) or spatial difference (in direction). The opponent intends the latter, which entails need.
The author uses the example of God's essence being opposed to the reality of space.
4
Grasp the final conclusion
Bodies can need spaces; God cannot need anything. Therefore, the spatial interpretation of 'mubayana' cannot apply to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى مباينا للعالم ، منفردا عنه ممتازا عنه وكونه تعالى كذلك ، لا يقتضي وجود أمر آخر سوى ذات الله تعالى ، فبطل قولكم إنه تعالى لو كان حاصلا في الحيز والجهة ، لكان مفتقرا إلى الغير. والذي بدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أنه لا نزاع في أن العالم مختص بالحيز والجهة ، وكونه كذلك لا معنى له إلا كون بعض الجواهر ممتازا عن البعض، منفرداً عنه وإذا عقلنا هذا المعنى ههنا ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ؟ والجواب : أما قوله : « الحيز والجهة ليس أمرا موجوداً في الأعيان ، فجوابه : إنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أنها أشياء موجودة في الأعيان ، وبعد قيام البراهين القاطعة على صحة هذه المقدمة ، فإنه لا يبقى في صحتها شك . وأما قوله : : المراد من كونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، كونه تعالى منفردا عن العالم ، أو ممتازاً عنه ، أو مباينا عنه . . فنقول : هذه الألفاظ كلها محتملة، فإن الانفراد والامتياز والمباينة قد تذكر ويراد بها المخالفة في الحقيقة والماهية. وذلك مما لا نزاع فيه ، ولكنه لا يقتضي الجهة . والدليل عليه : أن حقيقة ذات الله تعالى مخالفة لحقيقة الخيز والجهة وهذه المخالفة والمباينة ليست بالجهة. فإن امتياز ذات الله تعالى عن الجهة لا يكون بجهة أخرى. وإلا لزم التسلسل . وقد تذكر هذه الألفاظ ويراد بها الامتياز في الجهة والحيز ، وهو كون الشيء بحيث يصح أن يشار إليه : أنه ههنا أو هناك . وهذا مراد الخصم من قوله : إنه تعالى مباين عن العالم ومنفرد عنه ، وممتاز عنه . إلا أنا بينا بالبراهين القاطعة : أن هذا يقتضي كون ذلك الحيز أمرا موجودا [ ويقتضي أن يكون الحاصل في ذلك الحيز محتاجا إلى الحيز وقوله : « الأجسام حاصلة في الأحياز، فنقول : هذا (١) ] يقتضي أن تكون الأجسام محتاجة إلى الأحياز، وهذا غير ممتنع . أما كونه تعالى محتاجا إلى شيء آخر فهو ممتنع . فظهر الفرق
He, exalted, is separate from the world, unique from it, distinct from it, and His being thus does not necessitate the existence of another matter besides the essence of God, exalted. So your statement is false that if He were located in space and direction, He would be in need of another. And what indicates the correctness of what we mentioned is that there is no dispute that the world is specific to space and direction, and its being so has no meaning except that some atoms are distinct from others, unique from them. And if we understand this meaning here, why is the like of it not permissible in His being, exalted, specific to space and direction? The answer: As for his saying, 'Space and direction are not existent things in external entities,' the response is that we have demonstrated with conclusive proofs that they are existent things in external entities, and after the establishment of conclusive proofs of the correctness of this premise, no doubt remains about its correctness. And as for his saying, 'What is meant by His being, exalted, specific to space and direction is His being, exalted, unique from the world, or distinct from it, or separate from it,' we say: These expressions are all ambiguous, for uniqueness, distinction, and separation may be mentioned and what is meant by them is opposition in reality and essence. That is indisputable, but it does not necessitate direction. The proof of it is that the essence of God, exalted, is opposed to the essence of space and direction, and this opposition and separation is not by direction. For the distinction of the essence of God, exalted, from direction is not by another direction, otherwise infinite regress would follow. And these expressions may be mentioned and what is meant by them is distinction in direction and space, which is a thing's being such that it is correct to point to it as 'here' or 'there.' This is what the opponent intends by his saying that He, exalted, is separate from the world, unique from it, and distinct from it. Except that we have demonstrated with conclusive proofs that this necessitates that that space is an existing thing and necessitates that the one located in that space is in need of the space. And his saying, 'Bodies are located in spaces,' we say: This necessitates that bodies are in need of spaces, and this is not impossible. But that He, exalted, is in need of something else is impossible. So the difference is clear.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. The author begins by quoting an opponent's claim: that God's being 'mubayin' (separate) from the world does not imply a need for another existent, and thus the argument that if God were in space He would need something else is false. The author first clarifies that the world's being in space simply means that atoms are distinct from each other, and asks why the same could not apply to God. Then he addresses two specific points from the opponent. First, the opponent claims space and direction are not real things; the author asserts they have already proven they are real with conclusive proofs, so no doubt remains. Second, the opponent argues that what is meant by God's being in space is merely His distinctness from the world. The author responds by noting that terms like 'infirad' (uniqueness), 'imtiyaz' (distinction), and 'mubayana' (separation) are ambiguous. They can mean essential difference (which does not entail direction) or spatial distinction (which does). The opponent intends the latter. The author proves that essential difference does not require direction because God's essence is different from the reality of space itself, and that difference is not by a direction (otherwise infinite regress). However, spatial distinction would require an existing space and make the occupant in need of that space. Bodies need spaces — that is not impossible — but God's needing something else is impossible. Thus the difference between bodies and God is clear.

Key Terms
تسلسل (tasalsul, infinite regress)
مباينة (mubayana, separation)
انفراد (infirad, uniqueness)
امتياز (imtiyaz, distinction)
حيز (hayyiz, space)
جهة (jiha, direction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'mubayana' and 'imtiyaz' always refer to spatial separation, so if God is separate from the world, He must be in some direction.
Correction: The author explains that these terms can also mean essential difference, which does not entail direction or space. The opponent's intended spatial meaning leads to problems.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the opponent intend by saying God is 'mubayin'an al-‘alam' (separate from the world)?
A) Essential difference without spatial implication
B) Spatial separation such that one can point to Him as 'here' or 'there'
C) Metaphorical separation
D) Emotional separation

Key Takeaway
The author distinguishes between essential and spatial separation, proving that essential separation does not imply space, while spatial separation would entail a need for space which is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God being 'above' or 'near', do you catch yourself imagining a spatial location? How does this lesson challenge you to repent from such mental images?
?
You often use words like 'separate' or 'distinct' about God. Are you careful to avoid implying He needs space? What specific phrases will you now avoid or correct?
?
The passage shows that essential separation does not require direction. How does this truth change the way you approach God in your dua? Will you now focus more on His essence than on a sense of physical distance?

The Trilemma Against God Being in Space
The author presents a trilemma: if God were in space, He must be infinite, finite-in-some, or finite in all; all are impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical trilemma used to refute the claim that God is located in space, and why each spatial possibility leads to contradiction.

Core Idea
If God were in space, He would be infinite, finite, or mixed — all absurd.

The author presents a powerful logical argument that eliminates every possible way God could be in space. The argument is a trilemma: three mutually exclusive and exhaustive options, each shown to be impossible. By following this reasoning, the student sees why divine transcendence requires God to be beyond spatial categories. Let's examine the trilemma and its refutation of the first two cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the trilemma structure
Read the opening enumeration: three possibilities if God were in space. Notice that the author calls the enumeration (al-hasr) obvious.
The three cases are: infinite in all directions, finite in some and infinite in others, and finite in all directions.
2
Examine the refutation of the first case
The first case (God infinite in all directions) is refuted with four distinct reasons. Identify each reason and how it shows impossibility.
Reasons include: prior proofs against infinite dimensions, the world would be inside God, composition issues, and undermining proofs of finitude.
3
Examine the refutation of the second case
The second case (God finite in some directions, infinite in others) is refuted with two reasons. The passage begins the second reason but cuts off.
The first reason: the impossibility of infinite dimensions applies regardless of direction count.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the trilemma collectively proves that God cannot be in space. What does this teach about divine transcendence and the nature of space?
This argument is foundational in Islamic theology for establishing tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : لو كان تعالي مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، لكان إما أن يكون غير متناه من كل الجوانب ، أو يكون متناهيا من بعض الجوانب ، وغير متناه من سائر الجوانب ، أو يكون متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة فالقول بكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة باطل . أما الحصر فظاهر . وأما بيان فساد القسم الأول ، وهو كونه تعالى غير متناه من كل الجوانب فهو باطل لوجوه : الأول : الدلائل التي ذكرناها في امتناع وجود أبعاد غير متناهية . والثاني : إنه لو كان غير متناهي الذات، من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يلزم أن يكون العالم حاصلا في داخل ذات الله تعالى وهو محال . ولأنه يلزم أن تكون ذاته تعالى مخالطة للقاذورات والنجاسات ، وهو محال . الثالث : إنه إذا كان حاصلا في جميع الجوانب ، فالحيز الذي منه حصل في جانب العلو، إما أن يكون هو الذي حصل بعينه في السفل ، أو غيره . فإن كان الأول فقد حصل الشيء الواحد دفعة واحدة في أحياز غير متناهية . وذلك باطل . وإن كان الثاني لزم وقوع التركيب والتأليف في ذات الله ، وهو محال . الرابع : إنا إذا جوزنا وجود شيء له أبعاد غير متناهية ، فحينئذ لا يمكننا إقامة الدلالة على أن أجسام العالم متناهية ، لأن كل دليل يذكر في وجوب تناهي الأجسام ، فإنه بعينه ينتقض بوجود الله تعالى. فإنه على هذا التقدير ممتداً امتداداً لا نهاية له . وأما بيان فساد القسم الثاني وهو كونه متناهيا [ في بعض الجوانب ، وغير متناه (١) ] من سائر الجوانب. فهذا أيضا باطل لوجوه : الأول : إن الدلائل الدالة على وجود أبعاد غير متناهية يبطل القول بها سواء كان غير متناه من جانب واحد أو من كل الجهات والجوانب . والثاني : إن الجانب الذي هو غير متناه ، [ والجانب الذي هو متناه (٢) ] إما أن يكونا متساويين في تمام الماهية ، وإما أن لا يكونا كذلك . فإن كان الأول
The third argument: If He, exalted, were specific to space and direction, then it would be either that He is unbounded from all sides, or that He is bounded from some sides and unbounded from the rest of the sides, or that He is bounded from all sides. And the three divisions are false, so the statement that He, exalted, is specific to space and direction is false. As for the enumeration, it is obvious. As for the demonstration of the corruption of the first division, which is that He is unbounded from all sides, it is false for reasons: First: The proofs we have mentioned about the impossibility of the existence of unbounded dimensions. Second: If He were of unbounded essence from all sides, then it would follow that the world is located inside the essence of God, exalted, and that is impossible. And because it would follow that His essence, exalted, is mixed with filth and impurities, and that is impossible. Third: If He occupies all sides, then the space from which He occupies in the direction of above is either the same one that He occupies in the direction of below, or another. If the first, then a single thing occurs at once in unbounded spaces, and that is false. If the second, composition and arrangement would occur in the essence of God, and that is impossible. Fourth: If we allow the existence of a thing with unbounded dimensions, then we cannot establish the proof that the bodies of the world are finite, because every proof mentioned for the necessity of the finitude of bodies would be contradicted by the existence of God, exalted, for on this supposition He is extended with an infinite extension. As for the demonstration of the corruption of the second division, which is that He is bounded in some sides and unbounded in the rest of the sides, this too is false for reasons: First: The proofs indicating the existence of unbounded dimensions invalidate the claim, whether it is unbounded from one side or from all directions and sides. Second: The side that is unbounded and the side that is bounded are either equal in the entirety of essence or not. If the first...
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument (al-hujja al-thalitha) against the claim that God is in space. It is a logical proof structured as a trilemma. The author first states that if God were in space, He would necessarily be one of three cases: (1) infinite in all directions, (2) finite in some directions and infinite in others, or (3) finite in all directions. He then declares all three impossible, so the original claim is false. The enumeration of possibilities is obvious. The bulk of the passage refutes the first two cases. For the first case (infinite in all directions), the author gives four reasons: (1) This contradicts earlier proofs that infinite dimensions are impossible. (2) If God were infinite in all directions, the world would be inside Him, leading to mixing with impurities — impossible. (3) If God occupies all sides, the space above and below would either be identical (implying the same thing in infinite places) or different (implying composition in God) — both impossible. (4) Accepting an infinite being would undermine the proofs for the finitude of bodies, because those proofs would equally apply to God if He were extended infinitely. Then the author begins refuting the second case (finite in some sides, infinite in others). He gives two reasons: the first is that the impossibility of infinite dimensions applies regardless of whether it is one side or all sides. The second reason begins: the infinite side and the finite side must either be equal in essence or not. The text cuts off at 'if the first', leaving the argument incomplete. The overall argument is clear: all spatial possibilities for God lead to absurdities.

Key Terms
غير متناه (ghayr mutanahi)
متناه (mutanahi)
حيز (hayyiz)
جهة (jiha)
أبعاد (ab‘ad)
تركيب (tarkib)
تأليف (ta’lif)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God is infinite, He must occupy infinite space.
Correction: The argument shows that an infinite being in space leads to contradictions (e.g., world inside God, composition), so God cannot be in space at all.

Checkpoint
What is the first reason given for the corruption of the first division (God being infinite from all sides)?
A) It would make God composite
B) It contradicts earlier proofs that infinite dimensions are impossible
C) It would imply that God is mixed with impurities
D) It would undermine the proof of the finitude of bodies

Key Takeaway
The trilemma demonstrates that no spatial description can apply to God, preserving His absolute transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever imagined God as being 'above' the universe, like a king on a throne? What does this trilemma force you to reconsider about that mental picture, and how will you train your mind to think of God without spatial limits?
?
If God is not in any space, then He is not 'closer' to you in a mosque than in a marketplace. Does your worship reflect this truth, or do you unconsciously treat certain places as more 'holy' because you feel God is there? What will you change today?
?
The argument shows that spatial concepts about God lead to absurdities like God being mixed with filth. Are there any comfortable, familiar ways you think about God that are actually unworthy of His majesty? Will you abandon them, even if it feels unsettling?

Divine Transcendence

Refutation of the first possibility: God is infinite from all sides
Razi enumerates three possibilities and refutes the first (infinite from all sides) with four proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that God cannot be infinite in spatial extent.

Core Idea
Infinite spatial extent leads to absurdities like the world inside God.

Razi begins by laying out the three possible ways something could occupy space. The first is being infinite from all sides. He then proceeds to refute this with four powerful arguments, showing that such a concept is impossible for God.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration and first division
Read the first part of the Arabic text where Razi enumerates the three possibilities and begins to refute the first. Notice that he states the conclusion first, then provides reasons.
The author uses a very structured argumentative style.
2
Examine the first proof: infinite dimensions are impossible
Razi refers to earlier proofs against infinite dimensions. Think about why infinite dimensions are problematic in a theological context.
This proof relies on prior knowledge; if you haven't studied that, just note the logical move.
3
Analyze the second proof: the world would be inside God
If God is infinite, the entire universe would be within His essence, implying mixture with impurities. Consider why that is impossible for a transcendent being.
4
Reflect on the third and fourth proofs
The third proof shows that occupying all sides leads to either one thing in multiple places or composition. The fourth shows that allowing infinite dimensions undermines proofs of the world's finitude.
These are sophisticated logical arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سائر الجوانب ، أو يكون متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة فالقول بكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة باطل . أما الحصر فظاهر . وأما بيان فساد القسم الأول ، وهو كونه تعالى غير متناه من كل الجوانب فهو باطل لوجوه : الأول : الدلائل التي ذكرناها في امتناع وجود أبعاد غير متناهية . والثاني : إنه لو كان غير متناهي الذات، من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يلزم أن يكون العالم حاصلا في داخل ذات الله تعالى وهو محال . ولأنه يلزم أن تكون ذاته تعالى مخالطة للقاذورات والنجاسات ، وهو محال . الثالث : إنه إذا كان حاصلا في جميع الجوانب ، فالحيز الذي منه حصل في جانب العلو، إما أن يكون هو الذي حصل بعينه في السفل ، أو غيره . فإن كان الأول فقد حصل الشيء الواحد دفعة واحدة في أحياز غير متناهية . وذلك باطل . وإن كان الثاني لزم وقوع التركيب والتأليف في ذات الله ، وهو محال . الرابع : إنا إذا جوزنا وجود شيء له أبعاد غير متناهية ، فحينئذ لا يمكننا إقامة الدلالة على أن أجسام العالم متناهية ، لأن كل دليل يذكر في وجوب تناهي الأجسام ، فإنه بعينه ينتقض بوجود الله تعالى. فإنه على هذا التقدير ممتداً امتداداً لا نهاية له . وأما بيان فساد القسم الثاني وهو كونه متناهيا [ في بعض الجوانب ، وغير متناه ] من سائر الجوانب. فهذا أيضا باطل لوجوه : الأول : إن الدلائل الدالة على وجود أبعاد غير متناهية يبطل القول بها سواء كان غير متناه من جانب واحد أو من كل الجهات والجوانب والثاني : إن الجانب الذي هو غير متناه ، [ والجانب الذي هو متناه ] إما أن يكونا متساويين في تمام الماهية ، وإما أن لا يكونا كذلك . فإن كان الأول فحينئذ يصح على كل واحد من هذين الجانبين، عين ما يصح [ على الآخر ] وحينئذ يلزم أن يصير المتناهي غير متناه ، وأن يصير غير المتناهي متناهيا . وحينئذ يلزم أن يصح عليه التفرق والتمزق ، والنمو والذبول ، والزيادة والنقصان . وكل ذلك يدل على كونه محدثا متغيرا في نفس الذات . وأما إن كان الثاني فحينئذ يكون كل واحد من هذين الجزئين مخالفا للآخر بماهيته وحقيقته ، فتكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء المختلفة والأبعاض المتباينة بالطبيعة والماهية ، وذلك محال . وأيضا : فالجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، متصل بالجزء الذي هو متناه ، فغير المتناهي اتصل بالمتناهي بأحد جانبيه ، وذلك الجانب متناه ، إذ لو لم يكن هو من ذلك الجانب متناهيا لا متنع أن يصير متصلا . ذلك من الجانب بغيره ، وقد فرضناه متصلا به. هذا خلف. فيثبت أن الجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، وجب أن يكون متناهيا من أحد جانبيه ، مع أن ذلك الحيز طبيعة واحدة ، وحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا من أنه لا بد وأن تتشابه طبيعتا دينك الجانبين . وحينئذ يلزم صحة النمو والذبول ، والزيادة والنقصان . وذلك محال . وأما القسم الثالث ، وهو أن يقال : إنه متناه من كل الجوانب ، فنقول : هذا أيضاً محال لوجوه : الأول : إن كل ما كان متناهيا . فإن وقوعه أزيد مما وقع عليه بمقدار قليل ، أو أنقص منه بمقدار قليل : يكون جائزا . والعلم بهذا الجواز ضروري. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، كان وقوعه بذلك المقدار دون الأزيد والأنقص ، لابد وأن يكون الترجيح مرجح ، وتخصيص مخصص . وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يكون مفتقرا في [ وجوده إلى ] الفاعل المختار ، وهو على الله محال . الثاني : إنه لما أحاطت الحدود والنهايات به من كل الجوانب . فنقول : إن أحد نصفيه لا بد وأن يكون مغايرا للنصف الثاني منه ، ثم أحد ذينك
…all sides, or it is finite from all sides. And the three divisions are false. So the statement that He, exalted, is confined to place and direction is false. As for the enumeration [of divisions], it is obvious. As for the demonstration of the corruption of the first division—that He, exalted, is infinite from all sides—it is false for several reasons: First: the proofs we mentioned concerning the impossibility of the existence of infinite dimensions. Second: if He were infinite in essence from all sides, then it would follow that the world occurs inside the essence of Allah, exalted, and that is impossible. And because it would follow that His essence, exalted, is mixed with filth and impurities, and that is impossible. Third: if He occurs in all sides, then the place from which He occurs in the direction of above is either the very same that occurs in below, or other than it. If the first, then one thing occurs at once in infinite places, and that is false. If the second, then composition and arrangement in the essence of Allah follows, and that is impossible. Fourth: if we allow the existence of something with infinite dimensions, then we cannot establish proof that the bodies of the world are finite, because every proof mentioned concerning the necessary finitude of bodies would be equally invalidated by the existence of Allah, exalted. For on this assumption, He would be extended with infinite extension. And as for the demonstration of the corruption of the second division—that He is finite in some sides and infinite from the rest of the sides—this too is false for several reasons: First: the proofs indicating the existence of infinite dimensions invalidate the claim whether it is infinite from one side or from all sides and directions. Second: the side that is infinite and the side that is finite are either equal in the entirety of quiddity or not equal. If the first, then exactly what is valid for one of these two sides is valid for the other, and then it would follow that the finite becomes infinite and the infinite becomes finite. And then it would follow that division and tearing, growth and withering, increase and decrease are possible for it. All of that indicates that it is originated and changing in the essence itself. And if the second, then each of these two parts is different from the other in its quiddity and reality, so the essence of Allah, exalted, would be composed of different parts and members differing in nature and quiddity, and that is impossible. Also: the part that is infinite is connected to the part that is finite, so the infinite is connected to the finite on one of its sides, and that side is finite, for if it were not finite from that side, it would be impossible for it to become connected. That [connection] from the side with other than it, but we have assumed it connected to it. This is a contradiction. So it is established that the part that is infinite must be finite from one of its sides, yet that place is one nature, and then it returns to what we mentioned, that it is necessary that the natures of those two sides be similar. And then the possibility of growth and withering, increase and decrease follows. And that is impossible. And as for the third division—that it is said He is finite from all sides—we say: this is also impossible for several reasons: First: everything that is finite, its occurrence larger than what it is by a small amount, or smaller than it by a small amount, is possible. Knowledge of this possibility is necessary. And if the matter is so, then its occurrence in that quantity rather than the larger and smaller must have a preponderating factor and a specifying agent. And everything that is so is in need of a choosing agent for its existence, and that is impossible for Allah. Second: when boundaries and ends surround it from all sides, we say: one of its halves must be different from the other half, then one of those two…
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah (exalted) is in a place or direction (jiha). The author first states that there are only three possibilities for something that occupies space: it is either infinite from all sides, or finite from some sides and infinite from others, or finite from all sides. All three are impossible, thus the claim is false. The author then explains the corruption of each division in turn. For the first division (infinite from all sides), he gives four proofs: (1) earlier proofs that infinite dimensions are impossible; (2) if infinite, the entire world would be inside Allah's essence, and He would be mixed with impurities; (3) if He occupies all sides, then either the same place is both above and below (impossible for one thing to be in infinite places at once) or different places, leading to composition in His essence; (4) if something infinite exists, we could no longer prove that bodies are finite, as the same proofs would apply to Allah. For the second division (finite in some sides, infinite in others), he gives two proofs: (1) the proofs against infinite dimensions apply regardless of whether it is infinite from one side or all; (2) the infinite and finite sides are either equal in quiddity or not. If equal, then what holds for one holds for the other, so the finite becomes infinite and vice versa, leading to possibility of change and division. If not equal, then the essence becomes composed of different parts, impossible. Also, the infinite side connects to the finite side at a finite boundary, but then that side is finite, contradicting its infinity, and forcing the two sides to have similar natures, again leading to possibility of change. For the third division (finite from all sides), he gives two proofs: (1) anything finite could have been larger or smaller by a small amount, so its specific magnitude requires a choice by a free agent, but Allah is not dependent on such a cause; (2) if finite, then halves differ, leading to composition and change. The entire argument aims to prove Allah's transcendence above spatial attributes.

Key Terms
غير متناه
حيز
جهة
مخالطة
تركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that being 'in a place' could be attributed to God in a metaphorical sense without issue.
Correction: Razi shows that even the assumption of spatial presence leads to logical absurdities, so spatial attributes are absolutely denied of God.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three divisions of possible spatial occupancy that the author refutes?
A) Infinite from all sides
B) Finite from some sides and infinite from others
C) Finite from all sides
D) Nonexistent from all sides

Key Takeaway
The first division (infinite from all sides) is impossible because it leads to logical and theological absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah in your mind, do you ever unconsciously picture Him as being 'somewhere'—like above the heavens or in a certain direction? After reading this passage, how will you actively train yourself to remove any spatial imagery from your conception of Allah? What specific thought will you replace it with?
?
Razi argues that if God were infinite from all sides, He would be mixed with filth and impurities. This is a shocking consequence. Have you ever casually attributed physical properties to Allah without realizing the implications? Take a moment to repent for any unintentional disrespect in your thoughts, and commit tonight to studying more about Allah's transcendence (tanzih) so that your worship becomes more worthy of Him.
?
The fourth proof shows that allowing infinite dimensions would undermine the proof that the world is finite. This shows how one wrong assumption about Allah can collapse your entire worldview. Is there any wrong belief about Allah—even a small one—that you have been tolerating in your heart because it feels comfortable or familiar? What is it, and what step will you take this week to uproot it?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
10 min
Refutation of the second possibility: God is finite in some directions and infinite in others
Razi refutes the second division (finite in some sides, infinite in others) with two main arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that a being finite in some directions and infinite in others is impossible for God.

Core Idea
Mixing finitude and infinity in one being leads to contradiction and composition.

Having refuted the first possibility, Razi turns to the second: that God is finite in some directions and infinite in others. He presents two main arguments, showing that such a combination is impossible and implies change and composition in the divine essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the second division
Read the Arabic text that begins with 'وأما بيان فساد القسم الثاني'. Notice that Razi first states it is false, then gives reasons.
2
Understand the first reason
The first reason simply notes that the earlier arguments against infinite dimensions are not limited to all-sided infinity but apply to any infinite extension.
3
Analyze the second reason: equality or difference in quiddity
This is a detailed argument that either leads to the finite becoming infinite (if equal) or composition of different parts (if different). Both are impossible for God.
4
Reflect on the additional argument about connection
Razi argues that the infinite side must be finite at the point of connection, which contradicts its infinity and also leads to possibility of change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سائر الجوانب ، أو يكون متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة فالقول بكونه تعالى مختصا بالحيز والجهة باطل . أما الحصر فظاهر . وأما بيان فساد القسم الأول ، وهو كونه تعالى غير متناه من كل الجوانب فهو باطل لوجوه : الأول : الدلائل التي ذكرناها في امتناع وجود أبعاد غير متناهية . والثاني : إنه لو كان غير متناهي الذات، من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يلزم أن يكون العالم حاصلا في داخل ذات الله تعالى وهو محال . ولأنه يلزم أن تكون ذاته تعالى مخالطة للقاذورات والنجاسات ، وهو محال . الثالث : إنه إذا كان حاصلا في جميع الجوانب ، فالحيز الذي منه حصل في جانب العلو، إما أن يكون هو الذي حصل بعينه في السفل ، أو غيره . فإن كان الأول فقد حصل الشيء الواحد دفعة واحدة في أحياز غير متناهية . وذلك باطل . وإن كان الثاني لزم وقوع التركيب والتأليف في ذات الله ، وهو محال . الرابع : إنا إذا جوزنا وجود شيء له أبعاد متناه من جانب واحد أو من كل الجهات والجوانب والثاني : إن الجانب الذي هو غير متناه ، [ والجانب الذي هو متناه ] إما أن يكونا متساويين في تمام الماهية ، وإما أن لا يكونا كذلك . فإن كان الأول فحينئذ يصح على كل واحد من هذين الجانبين، عين ما يصح [ على الآخر ] وحينئذ يلزم أن يصير المتناهي غير متناه ، وأن يصير غير المتناهي متناهيا . وحينئذ يلزم أن يصح عليه التفرق والتمزق ، والنمو والذبول ، والزيادة والنقصان . وكل ذلك يدل على كونه محدثا متغيرا في نفس الذات . وأما إن كان الثاني فحينئذ يكون كل واحد من هذين الجزئين مخالفا للآخر بماهيته وحقيقته ، فتكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء المختلفة والأبعاض المتباينة بالطبيعة والماهية ، وذلك محال . وأيضا : فالجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، متصل بالجزء الذي هو متناه ، فغير المتناهي اتصل بالمتناهي بأحد جانبيه ، وذلك الجانب متناه ، إذ لو لم يكن هو من ذلك الجانب متناهيا لا متنع أن يصير متصلا . ذلك من الجانب بغيره ، وقد فرضناه متصلا به. هذا خلف. فيثبت أن الجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، وجب أن يكون متناهيا من أحد جانبيه ، مع أن ذلك الحيز طبيعة واحدة ، وحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا من أنه لا بد وأن تتشابه طبيعتا دينك الجانبين . وحينئذ يلزم صحة النمو والذبول ، والزيادة والنقصان . وذلك محال . وأما القسم الثالث ، وهو أن يقال : إنه متناه من كل الجوانب ، فنقول : هذا المقدار دون الأزيد والأنقص ، لابد وأن يكون الترجيح مرجح ، وتخصيص مخصص . وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يكون مفتقرا في [ وجوده إلى ] الفاعل المختار ، وهو على الله محال . الثاني : إنه لما أحاطت الحدود والنهايات Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah (exalted) is in a place or direction (jiha). The author first states that there are only three possibilities for something that occupies space: it is either infinite from all sides, or finite from some sides and infinite from others, or finite from all sides. For the second division (finite in some sides, infinite in others), he gives two proofs: (1) the proofs against infinite dimensions apply regardless of whether it is infinite from one side or all; (2) the infinite and finite sides are either equal in quiddity or not. If equal, then what holds for one holds for the other, so the finite becomes infinite and vice versa, leading to possibility of change and division. If not equal, then the essence becomes composed of different parts, impossible. Also, the infinite side connects to the finite side at a finite boundary, but then that side is finite, contradicting its infinity, and forcing the two sides to have similar natures, again leading to possibility of change. Checkpoint
According to Razi's second argument, what happens if the infinite and finite sides are equal in quiddity?
A) The finite side becomes infinite and the infinite becomes finite
B) The divine essence becomes composed of different parts
C) The infinite side becomes finite at the connection point
D) Both sides remain unchanged

Key Takeaway
The second division (finite in some sides, infinite in others) is impossible because it implies either change or composition in God's essence.

?

?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
8 min
Refutation of the third possibility: God is finite from all sides
Razi refutes the third division (finite from all sides) with two arguments; the second is incomplete.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that a spatially finite God is impossible.

Core Idea
A finite being requires a specific size, which implies dependence on a chooser, and internal division leads to composition.

The final possibility is that God is finite from all sides. Razi presents two arguments: first, any finite quantity could have been larger or smaller, requiring a cause for its specific size; second, finitude implies halves and parts, leading to composition. He begins the second argument, which is cut off in our passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the third division
Read the Arabic text starting with 'وأما القسم الثالث'. Note that Razi declares it impossible and gives reasons.
2
Understand the first reason: a finite size requires a specifying agent
If God has a specific finite size, why not slightly larger or smaller? That requires a chooser, making God dependent on external cause—impossible.
3
Analyze the second reason (incomplete): finitude implies halves and difference
Razi argues that a finite thing has two halves that must differ, leading to composition. The passage cuts off, but the implication is clear: this leads to impossibility.

والنقصان . وكل ذلك يدل على كونه محدثا متغيرا في نفس الذات . وأما إن كان الثاني فحينئذ يكون كل واحد من هذين الجزئين مخالفا للآخر بماهيته وحقيقته ، فتكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء المختلفة والأبعاض المتباينة بالطبيعة والماهية ، وذلك محال . وأيضا : فالجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، متصل بالجزء الذي هو متناه ، فغير المتناهي اتصل بالمتناهي بأحد جانبيه ، وذلك الجانب متناه ، إذ لو لم يكن هو من ذلك الجانب متناهيا لا متنع أن يصير متصلا . ذلك من الجانب بغيره ، وقد فرضناه متصلا به. هذا خلف. فيثبت أن الجزء الذي هو غير متناه ، وجب أن يكون متناهيا من أحد جانبيه ، مع أن ذلك الحيز طبيعة واحدة ، وحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا من أنه لا بد وأن تتشابه طبيعتا دينك الجانبين . وحينئذ يلزم صحة النمو والذبول ، والزيادة والنقصان . وذلك محال . وأما القسم الثالث ، وهو أن يقال : إنه متناه من كل الجوانب ، فنقول : هذا أيضاً محال لوجوه : الأول : إن كل ما كان متناهيا . فإن وقوعه أزيد مما وقع عليه بمقدار قليل ، أو أنقص منه بمقدار قليل : يكون جائزا . والعلم بهذا الجواز ضروري. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، كان وقوعه بذلك المقدار دون الأزيد والأنقص ، لابد وأن يكون الترجيح مرجح ، وتخصيص مخصص . وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يكون مفتقرا في [ وجوده إلى ] الفاعل المختار ، وهو على الله محال . الثاني : إنه لما أحاطت الحدود والنهايات به من كل الجوانب . فنقول : إن أحد نصفيه لا بد وأن يكون مغايرا للنصف الثاني منه ، ثم أحد ذينك
…all sides, or it is finite from all sides. And the three divisions are false. So the statement that He, exalted, is confined to place and direction is false. As for the enumeration [of divisions], it is obvious. As for the demonstration of the corruption of the first division—that He, exalted, is infinite from all sides—it is false for several reasons: First: the proofs we mentioned concerning the impossibility of the existence of infinite dimensions. Second: if He were infinite in essence from all sides, then it would follow that the world occurs inside the essence of Allah, exalted, and that is impossible. And because it would follow that His essence, exalted, is mixed with filth and impurities, and that is impossible. Third: if He occurs in all sides, then the place from which He occurs in the direction of above is either the very same that occurs in below, or other than it. If the first, then one thing occurs at once in infinite places, and that is false. If the second, then composition and arrangement in the essence of Allah follows, and that is impossible. Fourth: if we allow the existence of something with infinite dimensions, then we cannot establish proof that the bodies of the world are finite, because every proof mentioned concerning the necessary finitude of bodies would be equally invalidated by the existence of Allah, exalted. For on this assumption, He would be extended with infinite extension. And as for the demonstration of the corruption of the second division—that He is finite in some sides and infinite from the rest of the sides—this too is false for several reasons: First: the proofs indicating the existence of infinite dimensions invalidate the claim whether it is infinite from one side or from all sides and directions. Second: the side that is infinite and the side that is finite are either equal in the entirety of quiddity or not equal. If the first, then exactly what is valid for one of these two sides is valid for the other, and then it would follow that the finite becomes infinite and the infinite becomes finite. And then it would follow that division and tearing, growth and withering, increase and decrease are possible for it. All of that indicates that it is originated and changing in the essence itself. And if the second, then each of these two parts is different from the other in its quiddity and reality, so the essence of Allah, exalted, would be composed of different parts and members differing in nature and quiddity, and that is impossible. Also: the part that is infinite is connected to the part that is finite, so the infinite is connected to the finite on one of its sides, and that side is finite, for if it were not finite from that side, it would be impossible for it to become connected. That [connection] from the side with other than it, but we have assumed it connected to it. This is a contradiction. So it is established that the part that is infinite must be finite from one of its sides, yet that place is one nature, and then it returns to what we mentioned, that it is necessary that the natures of those two sides be similar. And then the possibility of growth and withering, increase and decrease follows. And that is impossible. And as for the third division—that it is said He is finite from all sides—we say: this is also impossible for several reasons: First: everything that is finite, its occurrence larger than what it is by a small amount, or smaller than it by a small amount, is possible. Knowledge of this possibility is necessary. And if the matter is so, then its occurrence in that quantity rather than the larger and smaller must have a preponderating factor and a specifying agent. And everything that is so is in need of a choosing agent for its existence, and that is impossible for Allah. Second: when boundaries and ends surround it from all sides, we say: one of its halves must be different from the other half, then one of those two…
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah (exalted) is in a place or direction (jiha). The author first states that there are only three possibilities for something that occupies space: it is either infinite from all sides, or finite from some sides and infinite from others, or finite from all sides. All three are impossible, thus the claim is false. The author then explains the corruption of each division in turn. For the first division (infinite from all sides), he gives four proofs: (1) earlier proofs that infinite dimensions are impossible; (2) if infinite, the entire world would be inside Allah's essence, and He would be mixed with impurities; (3) if He occupies all sides, then either the same place is both above and below (impossible for one thing to be in infinite places at once) or different places, leading to composition in His essence; (4) if something infinite exists, we could no longer prove that bodies are finite, as the same proofs would apply to Allah. For the second division (finite in some sides, infinite in others), he gives two proofs: (1) the proofs against infinite dimensions apply regardless of whether it is infinite from one side or all; (2) the infinite and finite sides are either equal in quiddity or not. If equal, then what holds for one holds for the other, so the finite becomes infinite and vice versa, leading to possibility of change and division. If not equal, then the essence becomes composed of different parts, impossible. Also, the infinite side connects to the finite side at a finite boundary, but then that side is finite, contradicting its infinity, and forcing the two sides to have similar natures, again leading to possibility of change. For the third division (finite from all sides), he gives two proofs: (1) anything finite could have been larger or smaller by a small amount, so its specific magnitude requires a choice by a free agent, but Allah is not dependent on such a cause; (2) if finite, then halves differ, leading to composition and change. The entire argument aims to prove Allah's transcendence above spatial attributes.

Key Terms
متناه
ترجيح
تخصيص
فاعل مختار
أجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that finitude is a safe attribute for God, avoiding the problems of infinity.
Correction: Razi shows that finitude also implies dependence on a specifying cause and internal composition, both incompatible with divinity.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, what is required for a finite being to have its specific size?
A) A preponderating factor and specifying agent
B) An infinite regress of causes
C) A natural necessity
D) Random chance

Key Takeaway
The third division (finite from all sides) is impossible because it requires a cause for its specific size and implies composition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every finite thing requires a specific size determined by a chooser, do you truly live as though your own existence—your height, lifespan, abilities—is chosen by God? What would change if you internalized this today?
?
The argument shows that relying on a 'specific size' implies dependence. In what areas of your life have you become self-reliant on your own 'specific amount' of wealth, health, or relationships, forgetting that God alone specifies and sustains them?
?
Razi's second argument hints that finitude leads to composition and thus imperfection. Are there 'halves' in your heart—loyalty divided between God and the world? How can you seek unity of purpose for His sake alone?

Divine Transcendence

First Case: Identical Sides Lead to Absurdity
First case: identical sides lead to contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why assuming the two sides of the divine essence are identical in nature leads to contradictions such as the finite becoming infinite and change being attributed to God.

Core Idea
Identical sides force the finite and infinite to interchange.

The argument begins by examining a hypothetical scenario where two imagined sides of God's essence are identical in nature. The author shows that this assumption forces impossible consequences that cannot apply to the Divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author sets up the hypothesis.
Focus on the conditional structure: 'if the two sides are identical...'
2
Identify the Consequence
Find the immediate consequence: what is valid for one side becomes valid for the other. This leads to the finite becoming infinite and vice versa.
This is a direct logical deduction from the identity assumption.
3
List the Absurdities
The author lists further absurdities: division, fragmentation, growth, withering, increase, decrease. Trace how each logically follows.
These are all signs of change and origination, impossible for God.
4
Connect to the Conclusion
The passage concludes that such consequences prove God would be originated and changing in His essence, which is impossible. Understand this as a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فحينئذ يصح على كل واحد من هذين الجانبين عين ما يصح على الآخر وحينئذ يلزم أن يصير المتناهي غير متناه وأن يصير غير المتناهي متناهيا. وحينئذ يلزم أن يصح عليه التفرق والتمزق والنمو والذبول والزيادة والنقصان. وكل ذلك يدل على كونه محدثا متغيرا في نفس الذات. وأما إن كان الثاني فحينئذ يكون كل واحد من هذين الجزئين مخالفا للآخر بماهيته وحقيقته، فتكون ذات الله تعالى مركبة من الأجزاء المختلفة والأبعاض المتباينة بالطبيعة والماهية، وذلك محال. وأيضا: فالجزء الذي هو غير متناه متصل بالجزء الذي هو متناه، فغير المتناهي اتصل بالمتناهي بأحد جانبيه، وذلك الجانب متناه، إذ لو لم يكن هو من ذلك الجانب متناهيا لامتنع أن يصير متصلا ذلك من الجانب بغيره، وقد فرضناه متصلا به. هذا خلف. فيثبت أن الجزء الذي هو غير متناه وجب أن يكون متناهيا من أحد جانبيه، مع أن ذلك الحيز طبيعة واحدة، وحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا من أنه لا بد وأن تتشابه طبيعتا هذين الجانبين. وحينئذ يلزم صحة النمو والذبول والزيادة والنقصان. وذلك محال.
Then it becomes valid for each one of these two sides exactly what is valid for the other, and then it necessarily follows that the finite becomes infinite and the infinite becomes finite. And then it necessarily follows that division, fragmentation, growth, withering, increase and decrease are valid for it. And all of that indicates that it is originated and changing in the essence itself. But if it is the second, then each one of these two parts is different from the other in its quiddity and reality, so the essence of God Most High would be composed of different parts and limbs diverse in nature and quiddity, and that is impossible. Also: the part that is infinite is connected to the part that is finite, so the infinite connected to the finite on one of its sides, and that side is finite, for if it were not finite on that side, it would be impossible for it to become connected from that side to another, and we have supposed it to be connected to it. This is a contradiction. So it is established that the part that is infinite must be finite on one of its sides, while that space is of a single nature, and then what we mentioned returns: that it is necessary for the natures of these two sides to be similar. And then the validity of growth, withering, increase and decrease necessarily follows. And that is impossible.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by hypothetical supposition. It begins by examining two sides (jaynayn) which likely refer to two imagined directions or parts of the divine essence if it were in a place. The author posits two cases: first, if the two sides are identical in nature, then what is valid for one is valid for the other, leading to absurd consequences: the finite becomes infinite and vice versa, and attributes like division, growth, and change become possible for God, which indicate origination and change in the essence itself—impossible for God. Second, if the two sides are different in quiddity, then God's essence would be composed of distinct parts, which is also impossible. The author reinforces this with an additional argument: the infinite part connected to the finite part must itself be finite on the connecting side, otherwise connection would be impossible. But the space is uniform in nature, so the two sides must be similar, leading back to the first case and its impossible consequences. Thus, any notion of God having parts or being in a direction leads to contradiction and is therefore impossible.

Key Terms
المتناهي
غير المتناهي
الجزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if two sides are identical, there is no problem.
Correction: Identity leads to interchange of properties, including finite and infinite, which is contradictory and entails change in God.

Checkpoint
What does the argument conclude if the two sides are identical?
A) They are both finite.
B) What is valid for one is valid for the other, leading to absurd consequences.
C) They are different in quiddity.
D) God's essence is simple.

Key Takeaway
Assuming identical sides in God's essence leads to contradictions that prove such a notion is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God, do you ever unconsciously assign Him a location or direction in your mind? How does this passage challenge that tendency, and what practical step can you take today to purify your belief?
?
This argument uses logical reasoning to defend God's transcendence. Are you content to rely on such proofs, or do you sometimes feel your heart is distant from the intellectual pursuit of tawhid? How can you blend this understanding with heartfelt awe?
?
If God cannot be divided or changed, then He is completely trustworthy in His promises. Is there an area in your life where you doubt God's consistency? How can meditating on His absolute simplicity strengthen your reliance on Him?

Second Case: Different Sides Imply Composition
Second case and additional argument: different sides imply composition; connection forces finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why different natures for the sides would imply composition in God, and why the infinite part must be finite on the connecting side, leading to further absurdities.

Core Idea
Different sides mean God's essence would be composite, and connection forces the infinite to be finite.

The second case explores what happens if the two sides are different in quiddity. The author then adds a second argument about the infinite part connected to the finite, showing that even the infinite must be finite on one side, contradicting its nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second case and the additional argument.
Notice the shift from 'أما إن كان الثاني'.
2
Analyze the Composition Argument
Understand that if the two parts are different in reality, then God's essence would be composed of diverse parts, which is impossible for a simple being.
Different quiddity means each part has its own essence.
3
Examine the Connection Argument
The infinite part is connected to the finite on one side. That side must be finite, otherwise connection is impossible. This is proven by contradiction.
This leads to a contradiction because the infinite would have a finite side.
4
See the Return to Absurdities
Because the space is uniform in nature, the two sides must be similar, which brings us back to the first case's absurd consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then it becomes valid for each one of these two sides exactly what is valid for the other, and then it necessarily follows that the finite becomes infinite and the infinite becomes finite. And then it necessarily follows that division, fragmentation, growth, withering, increase and decrease are valid for it. And all of that indicates that it is originated and changing in the essence itself. This is a contradiction. This passage presents a proof by hypothetical supposition. It begins by examining two sides (jaynayn) which likely refer to two imagined directions or parts of the divine essence if it were in a place. How does this proof expose the danger of such thoughts? What concrete step can you take today to purify your belief in God's perfect simplicity?
?

Will you act on that certainty by turning to Him directly, without relying on places or rituals as intermediaries?

Divine Transcendence

First Two Proofs Against Divine Finitude
First two proofs of five against divine finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two arguments showing that God cannot be finite from all sides: the necessity of a particularizer for the specific size and the implication of divisibility from having halves.

Core Idea
Finitude requires a cause for precise size and implies composition—both impossible for God.

The author begins the third division of possible spatial relations for God—being finite from all sides. He presents five proofs. The first two focus on the logical consequences of finitude: a finite object's specific size demands a preponderant cause, and having halves forces separability. Let's examine these arguments carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text from 'وأما القسم الثالث' up to the end of the second proof. Try to grasp the flow of the argument without yet analyzing details.
Notice the author's style: he states the hypothesis, then refutes it with numbered reasons.
2
Understand the first proof
Identify how the author argues that a finite being's actual size, which could have been slightly more or less, requires a preponderant (murajjih) and a particularizer (mukhassis). This makes it dependent on a free agent, impossible for God.
The key phrase: 'فيكون مفتقرا في وجوده إلى الفاعل المختار'
3
Understand the second proof
Focus on the argument that a finite being from all sides has halves that must touch each other on both faces due to uniform nature, leading to the possibility of separation and composition—impossible for God.
The conclusion: 'ثبت جواز التفرق والتمزق... وذلك محال'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث وهو أن يقال: إنه متناه من كل الجوانب، فنقول: هذا أيضاً محال لوجوه: الأول: إن كل ما كان متناهيا، فإن وقوعه أزيد مما وقع عليه بمقدار قليل، أو أنقص منه بمقدار قليل: يكون جائزا. والعلم بهذا الجواز ضروري. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، كان وقوعه بذلك المقدار دون الأزيد والأنقص، لابد وأن يكون له مرجح، وتخصيص مخصص. وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يكون مفتقرا في وجوده إلى الفاعل المختار، وهو على الله محال. الثاني: إنه لما أحاطت الحدود والنهايات به من كل الجوانب. فنقول: إن أحد نصفيه لا بد وأن يكون مغايرا للنصف الثاني منه، ثم أحد ذينك النصفين، لا بد وأن يماس النصف الثاني منه بأحد وجهيه دون الوجه الثاني، وكما صح على النصف الأول أن يماس النصف الثاني منه بأحد وجهيه، وجب عليه أن يماسه بوجهه الثاني، ضرورة أن كل واحد من وجهيه على طبيعة واحدة، وكل ما صح على الشيء، وجب أن يصح على مثله. ومتى ثبت ذلك، ثبت جواز التفرق والتمزق، والاجتماع والافتراق عليه. وذلك محال. الثالث: إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب، فحينئذ يكون متناهيا من جهة فوق، وحينئذ تكون الأحياز الفارغة حاصلة فوقه. فإذا خلق الله في تلك الأحياز الفارغة عالما آخر، فحينئذ يلزم وقوع ذلك العالم فوق الباري، ووقوع الباري تحت العالم. وذلك محال بالاتفاق. الرابع: إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب، فحينئذ يصح من الله تعالى أن يخلق أجساما متصلة بتلك الذات من كل الجوانب، وحينئذ يصح عليه الاجتماع والافتراق. وذلك يدل على الحدوث. الخامس: إنا إذا جوزنا في الشيء الذي يكون محدودا متناهيا من كل الجوانب: أن يكون إلها لهذا العالم، فحينئذ لا يمكننا البتة أن نقطع بأن الشمس والقمر ليسا إلهين لهذا العالم، لأنه لا عيب فيهما إلا أحد أمور ثلاثة: أحدهما: التناهي. والثاني: كونه مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض. والثالث: كونه قابلا للحركة والسكون، فإذا جوزنا هذه الثلاثة في حق الإله تعالى فحينئذ لا يمكننا جعل هذه الأشياء عيبا في الإلهية. وحينئذ لا يمكننا القدح في إلهية الشمس والقمر وسائر الكواكب. بل على هذا التقدير، فلعل إله العالم هو العرش نفسه، من غير حاجة إلى إثبات شيء آخر، معلوم إن كل ما يلزم منه هذا القول، فهو باطل بإجماع من العقلاء. فيثبت بما ذكرنا: أن إله العالم لو كان حاصلا في الجهة والحيز، لوجب وقوعه على أحد هذه الأقسام وثبت بالدليل فسادها بأسرها، فوجب القطع بأنه يمتنع كون الإله عز وجل حاصلا في الحيز والجهة.
As for the third division, which is to say: He is finite from all sides, we say: This too is impossible for several reasons: First: Everything that is finite, its existence being a little more than what it is, or a little less than it, is possible. And knowledge of this possibility is necessary. And if the matter is so, then its existence in that amount rather than the more or the less necessarily requires a preponderant and a particularizing specifier. And everything like that is dependent in its existence upon a free agent, and that is impossible for God. Second: When boundaries and ends surround it from all sides, we say: One of its halves must be different from the other half of it, then one of those two halves must touch the other half of it on one of its faces without the second face, and just as it is valid for the first half to touch the second half of it on one of its faces, it must also touch it on its second face, necessarily because each of its faces is of the same nature, and whatever is valid for a thing must be valid for its like. And when that is established, the validity of division and fragmentation, and conjunction and separation upon it is established. And that is impossible. Third: If it is finite from all sides, then it is finite from the direction above, and then empty spaces exist above it. So if God creates another world in those empty spaces, then it necessarily follows that that world is above the Creator, and the Creator is below that world. And that is impossible by consensus. Fourth: If it is finite from all sides, then it is valid for God Most High to create bodies connected to that essence from all sides, and then conjunction and separation become valid for it. And that indicates origination. Fifth: If we allow for a thing that is limited and finite from all sides to be a god for this world, then we cannot at all be certain that the sun and moon are not gods for this world, because there is no defect in them except one of three things: one: finitude; second: being composed of parts and limbs; third: being capable of movement and rest. So if we allow these three with respect to the divine, then we cannot make these things a defect in divinity. And then we cannot impugn the divinity of the sun, moon and the rest of the planets. Rather, on this assumption, perhaps the god of the world is the Throne itself, without needing to establish anything else. It is known that everything that necessitates this statement is false by consensus of the rational. So it is established by what we have mentioned: that if the god of the world were in direction and space, he would necessarily fall under one of these divisions, and the proof established the corruption of all of them, so it is necessary to decide that it is impossible for God, Mighty and Exalted, to be in space and direction.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents five distinct proofs against the third division—the hypothesis that God is finite from all sides. The author systematically refutes each one. Proof One argues that a finite being could have been larger or smaller, so its actual size requires a cause that particularizes it, making it dependent on a free agent—impossible for God. Proof Two shows that finitude implies having halves that are different and, due to the uniformity of nature, each half must touch the other on both faces, leading to separability and composition—impossible. Proof Three states that if God is finite, there could be empty space above Him, and if God creates another world there, that world would be above God, which is absurd. Proof Four says that if finite, God could create bodies attached to His essence from all sides, making Him subject to conjunction and separation—indicating origination. Proof Five argues that if finitude, composition, and motion are allowed in God, then we cannot deny divinity to celestial bodies like the sun and moon, as they share these attributes; this leads to absurd polytheism. The passage concludes that since all possible divisions (finite from one side, both sides, or all sides) have been proven false, it is impossible for God to be in place or direction.

Key Terms
متناه
مرجح
مخصص
فاعل مختار
نصفين
مماسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Finitude could be acceptable for God if He is a special body not subject to physical laws.
Correction: The proofs show that finitude logically entails dependence on a cause for specific size and the possibility of division, regardless of special status.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what does the possibility of a finite being being larger or smaller necessitate?
A) That it must be eternal
B) That it requires a preponderant and specifier for its specific size
C) That it is simple and indivisible
D) That it can exist without a cause

Key Takeaway
The first two proofs establish that divine finitude entails dependence on a cause for precise size and implies composition, both incompatible with God's nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your own existence is precisely determined by God's free choice, not by chance or necessity, how does that reshape how you see even the smallest details of your life? What can you do today to actively acknowledge your complete dependence on Him?
?
The proof shows that a finite being could have been different — slightly larger or smaller. In your life, do you often wish your circumstances were different? How does knowing that God's precise decree is from a free and perfect Agent help you submit to His will?
?
If finitude leads to composition and division, and God is absolutely simple and indivisible, then what does that say about your own understanding of God? Are there ways you have been treating God's attributes as separate pieces rather than a unified whole? What step can you take today to worship Him as truly One?

Third and Fourth Proofs: Spatial and Compositional Impossibilities
Third and fourth proofs against divine finitude from all sides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third and fourth arguments against God being finite: the problem of empty space above leading to something above God, and the possibility of attaching created bodies.

Core Idea
Finitude allows something to be above God or bodies to attach, both absurd consequences.

The author continues his refutation with two more proofs that build directly on the concept of finitude. The third proof considers the logical consequence of empty space above a finite God, and the fourth proof examines what happens if God creates bodies adjacent to His essence. Both lead to impossible conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the third proof
Read the Arabic for the third proof carefully. Notice how the author uses a hypothetical scenario (creating another world) to show an absurd outcome.
Key phrase: 'يلزم وقوع ذلك العالم فوق الباري'
2
Understand the fourth proof
Read the fourth proof and note that it builds on the idea that if God is finite, He could create bodies touching His essence from all sides, making Him subject to conjunction and separation.
The conclusion: 'ذلك يدل على الحدوث'
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why these consequences are impossible for God: something above the Creator undermines His supremacy, and composition/origination contradicts His eternal nature.

Commentary
This passage presents five distinct proofs against the third division—the hypothesis that God is finite from all sides. The author systematically refutes each one. ?

Divine Transcendence

Fifth Proof: Collapse of Distinction Between God and Creatures
Fifth proof and conclusion against divine finitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth proof: if finitude is allowed in God, we cannot distinguish Him from celestial bodies, leading to polytheism.

Core Idea
Accepting finitude makes the sun and moon possible gods.

The final proof takes a different approach. Instead of arguing from logical impossibilities, it shows the unacceptable theological consequences: if we allow finitude (and thus composition and motion) in God, we cannot deny divinity to objects like the sun, moon, or the Throne. This reductio ad absurdum closes the case against divine finitude.

Guided Path
1
Read the fifth proof and conclusion
Read the Arabic from 'الخامس' to the end. Notice how the author lists the three attributes that disqualify celestial bodies from being gods.
Key phrase: 'لا يمكننا البتة أن نقطع بأن الشمس والقمر ليسا إلهين'
2
Understand the argument
The proof shows that if finitude, composition, and motion are acceptable for God, then celestial bodies, which also have these attributes, cannot be ruled out as gods. This leads to absurd consequences, even suggesting the Throne could be God.
3
Learn the conclusion
The author concludes that since all divisions (finite from one side, both sides, all sides) have been proven false, God cannot be in direction or space at all.
Final sentence: 'يثبت بما ذكرنا: أن إله العالم لو كان حاصلا في الجهة والحيز، لوجب وقوعه على أحد هذه الأقسام وثبت بالدليل فسادها بأسرها، فوجب القطع بأنه يمتنع كون الإله عز وجل حاصلا في الحيز والجهة.'

As for the third division, which is to say: He is finite from all sides, we say: This too is impossible for several reasons: First: Everything that is finite, its existence being a little more than what it is, or a little less than it, is possible. Commentary

Proof Three states that if God is finite, there could be empty space above Him, and if God creates another world there, that world would be above God, which is absurd. Proof Four says that if finite, God could create bodies attached to His essence from all sides, making Him subject to conjunction and separation—indicating origination. Proof Five argues that if finitude, composition, and motion are allowed in God, then we cannot deny divinity to celestial bodies like the sun and moon, as they share these attributes; this leads to absurd polytheism. The passage concludes that since all possible divisions (finite from one side, both sides, or all sides) have been proven false, it is impossible for God to be in place or direction.

Key Terms
كوكب
عرش
عيب
إلهية
جهة
حيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accepting that God has a size does not automatically make the sun or moon gods because they have other imperfections.
Correction: The proof shows that if finitude, composition, and motion are not defects in God, then they cease to be defects anywhere, removing the basis for distinguishing God from creatures.

Checkpoint

A) To prove God's existence
B) To deny divinity to the sun and moon
C) To attribute creation to God
D) To believe in the Throne

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof uses a slippery slope to show that allowing any finitude in God collapses the distinction between Creator and creation, proving that God must be beyond space and direction.

In what subtle ways have you compared Allah to His creation in your heart—like assuming He feels emotions exactly as humans do—and what will you do to purify that belief?
?
The proof shows that compromising even slightly on God's transcendence opens the door to shirk. Is there any area of your life where you act as if Allah is limited—like not trusting His provision, fearing human judgment more than His, or thinking He is 'too busy' for your small problems? The Third Argument: Finitude Implies a World Above God
Presents the third argument against divine spatiality: empty space above leads to a world above God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that God cannot be spatially finite because it would allow a world above Him.

Core Idea
Spatial finitude of God leads to an absurd hierarchy.

This lesson presents the third argument from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah against the idea that God occupies space. The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: assuming God is finite in space leads to the possibility of a world above Him, which is impossible. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical chain: if finite from all sides → finite above → empty space above → possible creation → world above God.
The argument assumes God is in space for the sake of refutation.
2
Identify the absurd consequence
The argument concludes that it would be impossible for God to be below another world. Why is that absurd? Because God is the Highest, and nothing can be above Him.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
This argument shows that God cannot be in space at all. It reinforces the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يكون متناهيا من جهة فوق ، وحينئذ تكون الأحياز الفارغة حاصلة فوقه. فإذا خلق الله في تلك الأحياز الفارغة عالما آخر ، فحينئذ يلزم وقوع ذلك العالم فوق الباري ، ووقوع الباري تحت العالم . وذلك محال بالاتفاق
The third: If He is finite from all sides, then He is finite from the direction above, and then empty spaces are above Him. So if God creates another world in those empty spaces, then it would follow that that world is above the Creator, and the Creator is under the world. And that is impossible by consensus.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an argument (reductio ad absurdum) against the claim that God exists in space. It assumes for the sake of argument that God is finite and spatially located. If so, there would be empty space above Him. God, being omnipotent, could create another world in that empty space. That world would then be above God, and God would be underneath it. This is absurd because God is the Highest, and nothing can be above Him. Therefore, the premise that God is in space is false.

The Fourth Argument: Spatiality Implies Composition and Contingency
Presents the fourth argument: finitude allows bodily attachment, implying composition and temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why spatial finiteness would imply composition and temporality for God, and how this argument supports divine transcendence.

Core Idea
If God were in space, He could be composed—making Him contingent, not divine.

The fourth argument against God being in space builds on the idea of finitude. If God has spatial boundaries, it becomes possible for Him to be attached to other things, which would make Him composite and subject to separation. Both are signs of contingency and temporality, which cannot apply to the eternal Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to see its logical flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if finite... then...'.
The argument is concise; each phrase carries a step.
2
Identify the logical chain
Break down the argument: finitude → possible attachment → possible composition/separation → indicates temporality. Understand why composition and separation are signs of contingency.
Composition requires parts, and parts can be separated—both impossible for a necessary being.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: If God were composite, would He be dependent on His parts? How does that contradict necessary existence? This shows why God cannot be in space.
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يصح من الله تعالى أن يخلق أجساما متصلة بتلك الذات من كل الجوانب ، وحينئذ يصح عليه الاجتماع والافتراق . وذلك يدل على الحدوث
The fourth: If He is finite from all sides, then it is possible for God (exalted) to create bodies connected to that essence from all sides, and then composition and separation would be possible for Him. And that indicates temporality (ḥudūth).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is another argument against God being in space. If God were finite and located, He would have boundaries. It would then be possible for God to create bodies attached to His essence on all sides. This would result in God being composed of parts (composition) and capable of separation (being divided). Both composition and the possibility of separation are characteristics of contingent, temporal beings. Since God is necessarily eternal and not contingent, He cannot be in space.

Key Terms

الافتراق
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Composition in itself is not a problem for God; it is merely a structural feature.
Correction: In Islamic theology, composition implies dependency on parts and the possibility of separation, both of which are signs of contingency and temporality. Since God is necessary and eternal, He cannot be composite.

Checkpoint

D) Because space is empty.

Key Takeaway
If God were in space, He would be subject to composition and separation—marks of contingency—so the eternal, necessary Creator cannot be spatial.
